PREFACE
The literary dialects spanned by a vast period
starting from the early Vedic to the Classical
Sanskrit are placed under one linguistic period
called Old Indo-Aryan. However, the language of all
these literary texts is not uniform. The language
of the Epics differs from that of the Vedic and
of Classical Sanskrit. The Epic pecutiarities have
been explained as irreglarities or un-paninian
forms. The language of the Epics. in fact, repre-
sents a particular variety of popular Sanskrit which
was current much earlier than Panini's time. Epic
language shares a number of Middle lndo-Aryan
features. Various schoiars expressed in the past
the need for a systematic and exhaustivs study of
the language of the Epics. Such a study will
greatly contribute to our understanding of the
history of the syntax of Indo-Aryan and also
increase our knowledge of Middle Indo-Aryan.
The present work makes a comparative study
of the peculiarities of the Epic language with that
Aryan on the other, in the introduction. Besides
giving a detailed description of the Epic language.
this Work points out, at relevant places, the Epic
peculiarities and idioms which differ from those
noted down by Panini. This work, it is hoped, will
fulfil a long-felt need.
This book is a revised version of my thesis
submitted to the University of Pune in  963 and
approved by the University for the Degree of
Doctor of Philosophyin 1964. Grateful acknowle-
dgerment is due to the authorities of the University
of Pune for permission to publish the thesis.

<!-- page 6 -->

INTRODUCTION
Syntax is that branch of the study of the language which
deals with the use of the grammatical forms, agreement among
some of these forms and the mode of their agreement in respect
of the meaning conveyed by a sentence. The words may be
either inflected such as noun etc., or uninflected like prepositions.
adverbs and particles.
Valuable contributions have been made in this branch of the
study of the ianguage by Western as well as Indian scholars
taking up a particular aspect of syntax or confining the investiga-
tion to a certain period of time. It may not be out of place to
mention some of those scholars who have contributed to syntactic
study. B. Delbrik, J. S. Speyer, A. A. Macdonell, A. B. Keith,
J. Gonda, H. Oertel and a few oithers have contributed to the
study of the Vedic syntax. Syntactical study of the Middle
Indo-Aryan languages has been done by Sukumar Sen, A. M.
Ghatage, M. A. Mehendale and a few others. J. S. Speiyer's
"Sanskrit Syntax' gives a detailed account of the syntax of the
Classical Sanskrit.
The syntactic study of the Epic language in a systematic
manner has long been a desideratum. The present work attempts
to make an exhaustive study of the syntax of the language of the
Epics covering all its aspects. Considering the voluminous nature
of the two Epics, the study is restricted to two parvans (Sabha
and Udyoga) and two cantos (Ayodhya and Yuddha) of the
Mahabharata and Ramayana respectively.
Chronologically the Epics stand somewhat on the same level
as early Classical Sanskrit and of course, later than the Vedic
period. On the other hand, since the Epic poetry is supposed to
have originally developed in circles which stood outside Brahma-
nical influence, they may be considered as standing midway
between the Brahmanical Sanskrit and the Middle Indo-Aryan
languages. The Classical Sanskrit shows in some respects Prakri-
tic inffuence. As the Epic language forms the transitional stage
a comparative study of the Vedic and the Epic language will

Sanskrit has three numbers, viz. singular, dual and plural.
ded as the use of singular in place of the usual plural :
Dual is used to express those objects which always go in pairs
tayor devanam atrasit pranayor (M. 2.61.60) -- They staked

their lives; pranayos tu panam krtva (M. 5.35.14) -- Staking

(our) lives; pranayor vipanavahe (M. 5.35.19) - Let us stake our

Jives.

(B) PAST TENSE
specified period of time in the forest as had been stipulated;
In Vedic Sanskrit there are three tenses denoting a past action,
pandavan yadi gacchami kim mam ksatram vadisyari (M. 5.144. 10)
viz , the imperfect, the perfect and the aorist. The imperfect
 If I go to the Pandavas, what would all the ksatriyas say ?
denotes past action done previous to the current day (Pan. I.2.
imam api hatam kubjam yadi janati raghavah tvam ca mam caiva
1l l), hence at a time removed from this day. The perfect denotes

(2) Periphrastic future is used in conditional sentence like
simple future, expressing one action depending upon another as
effect upon cause. The periphrastic future is generally used in
the protasis and the simple future is mostly employed in the
apodosis of the conditional sentence.1 Thus :
atas ced anyatha karta dhartarastro 'nupayavit antam nunam

ksatriya race; araksasam imam lokam kartasmi nisitaih saraih na
cec charanam abhyesi tam adaya tu maithilim (R. 6.41.67) -- I
shall rid the earth of raksasas with my pointed shafts, if thou
to me.
(3) When a person swears to do an action, periphrastic future
is employed. Thus :

(E) POTENTIAL PASSIVE PARTICIPLE
The potential passive participle is used in the sense of what
should be done or ought to be done. They signify precept, duty,
necessity, etc., like the potential mood.

(2) PARTICLES OF NEGATION

Sanskrit has two negative particles, viz., na and ma, of which
ramah (R. 6.12.34) -- It is fortunate that Rama did not slay thee.

use the negative particle na in any place in a sentence. Generally

paid her every homage and cast thyself at my feet.

yadi cet or yadi (if)
evam te jnatipaksasya sreyas caiva bhavisyati yadi ced bharato
dharmat pitryan rajyam avapsyati (R. 2.8.34) -.-- In case Bharata
rightly secures his paternal throne, then only will the welfare of
those (like myself) belonging to the side of your parents be
ensured; sarvam tad upapadyetha jahyam ced yadi jivitam (R.
6.20.33) --- (The conseguence of all evil deeds that I have done)
fall on thee, if I lose my life.

kurun sarvan (M. 5.70.87) -- If, after all, they do me any injury,
then I will consume all the Kurus; atha cet satyavacanam
